Good to see a lot of people commending Francis. Even boxing/Fury fans are unanimously conceding they felt Francis won.   Personally, I'm the opposite. I'm an MMA fan to the core - don't watch much boxing aside from major fights and of course the MMA crossover spectacles. I went into this rooting for Francis, but strongly suspecting Fury would win.  I knew Francis had the power to get his respect, but didn't think the technical discrepancy would allow him to make it happen.  First off, I was utterly shocked at how well Francis fought. On a technical level, I actually think he's a better boxer than Wilder. I always compared him to Wilder in terms of what he would bring to professional boxing; a power hitter who can beat top competitors even with a technical disadvantage due to his power. But now I genuinely believe Ngannou would be the more technical boxer between the two if they fought.   But anyways, regarding the fight itself, I think I went into it with a built in safeguard to help me deal with any potential anger/feeling of "let down" that comes from judges scoring. It feels to me that the few major boxing fights I have tuned in for, the scoring always leans to the more famous/high ranked fighter. Maybe it was some bad experience watching Floyd lol, but whoever's obviously getting attacked more, but stays defensive and boring, and lands a few peppery shots wins the round.   So in order to avoid super disappointment for a potential robbery, I tried to watch this from a strictly scoring standpoint. And as fucking stoked and excited as I was whenever Francis landed ANYTHING - I would try to ground myself with "okay, I gotta remember Fury's getting his licks in too, not all of these are hitting Fury cleanly, and the judges are probably giving him these close rounds". So even though the true fan in me felt Francis was winning, the "but boxing scoring likes to ruin the vibe" party pooper side of me kept pocketing all the rounds for Fury that didn't clearly favor Ngannou.   However, this forced "be ready for a robbery" mindset sort of allowed me to score from a very open minded standpoint. And then, I started noticing that in all these moments where I'm screaming in joy for Ngannou... Fury was ducking the worst of the combo. Popping Francis in the head to close off the exchange. Snapping the jab during the dead time between moments when I would usually be otherwise talking to my friends about how well Francis is doing. And come the end, I felt like Fury edged 6 rounds with his jab and simply landing a few more.   Yes, I was still forcing myself to value Fury's brief moments and jabs more than I usually would as a Francis fan. I was still forcing myself not to score Francis' combos too heavily when I noticed Fury rolling with the punches and not eating them flush. So I'm by no means claiming this was the type of assessment wherein I'd put my reputation on the line with this claim that Francis won. I'm not even sure I believe that at all - especially after seeing these comments. So I do want to re-watch it.  But honestly F the outcome. F the result. Francis FREAKING Ngannou just went out there and brought it to the Undisputed HW Boxing Champ for 10 rounds, knocked him down, had the more profound moments, took him to a split decision and arguably looked like the superior boxer - in his FIRST EVER boxing match. Absolutely incredible and a HUGE win for MMA. This should be the narrative and talking point about this fight. Huge W for Francis and MMA.  Definitely helps earn back some respect for our sport and the skill level some of our fighters have in the striking department - and that many of these MMA guys could possibly give top 5 boxers a run for their money if they dedicated a year to it. Heck, before tonight, people didn't even consider Ngannou to have the most skillful hands IN MMA outside of his offensive power, and he arguably showcased cleaner looking technical defense than the best boxer alive did tonight.
